# Architecture Document: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/envoy--1d0ba73a (mirror of envoyproxy/envoy)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Task

Produce an architecture document for Envoy's **HTTP Connection Manager** (HCM) subsystem. The document must explain how the major components interact to process an HTTP request from arrival on a downstream connection through to upstream dispatch. Do not simply list APIs — explain the **design**, **data flow**, and **extension points**.

## Scope

Your document must cover these four components and how they work together:

### 1. ConnectionManagerImpl
The central network filter that owns the connection lifecycle. Explain:
- How it implements `Network::ReadFilter` to receive raw bytes
- How it creates and manages `ActiveStream` objects for each HTTP request
- Its role in codec creation (lazy codec instantiation for H1/H2 vs. H3)
- Connection-level concerns: drain decisions, overload management, watermark-based flow control

### 2. FilterManager and the HTTP Filter Chain
The per-stream filter chain execution engine. Explain:
- The decoder filter chain (request path) and encoder filter chain (response path)
- How `FilterChainFactory` creates filters for each stream
- Filter iteration: how `decodeHeaders`/`decodeData`/`decodeTrailers` propagate through decoder filters
- How filters can stop iteration, modify headers, or send local replies
- The distinction between `StreamDecoderFilter`, `StreamEncoderFilter`, and `StreamFilter` (dual)

### 3. Router Filter
The terminal decoder filter that forwards requests upstream. Explain:
- Route selection: how the router uses `RouteConfiguration` to pick a cluster
- How it obtains an HTTP connection pool from `ClusterManager`
- Upstream request lifecycle: `UpstreamRequest` creation, retry logic, timeout handling
- Shadow routing and hedged request support (if applicable)

### 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity
The upstream connection pool and cluster management layer. Explain:
- How `ClusterManagerImpl` provides connection pools per cluster
- Load balancing: how the router obtains a host from the cluster's load balancer
- Connection pool mechanics: the relationship between logical connection pools and physical connections
- How health checking and outlier detection feed back into the load balancer

## Document Requirements

1. **Component Responsibilities** — what each component owns
2. **Data Flow** — the path of an HTTP request from downstream bytes to upstream dispatch, and the response path back
3. **Extension Points** — where users extend Envoy (HTTP filters, cluster extensions, load balancers, access loggers)
4. **Error Handling** — how errors at each stage (codec errors, filter errors, upstream failures) are handled
5. **relevant source files** — reference the actual source files in the envoyproxy/envoy repository

## Anti-Requirements

- Do NOT generate a simple API listing or header-file dump
- Do NOT fabricate class names or file paths that don't exist in the repository
- Do NOT cover Envoy components outside the HCM request path (e.g., xDS config delivery, listener management)

     1→# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture
     2→
     3→## Overview
     4→
     5→The HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is Envoy's core subsystem for processing HTTP requests from downstream clients, transforming them according to configured routing and filtering rules, and forwarding them to upstream services. This document explains the design and interactions between the four major components that implement this functionality.
     6→
     7→The HCM request processing pipeline follows this flow:
     8→1. **Raw bytes arrive** on a downstream TCP connection
     9→2. **ConnectionManagerImpl** (Network::ReadFilter) receives and decodes them
    10→3. **ActiveStream** is created per request and manages per-stream state
    11→4. **FilterManager** executes the configured HTTP filter chain
    12→5. **Router Filter** (terminal decoder filter) performs route selection and upstream forwarding
    13→6. **UpstreamRequest** manages the upstream connection and stream lifecycle
    14→7. **ClusterManager** and **ThreadLocalCluster** provide connection pools to upstream services
    15→8. **Responses flow back** through the filter chain in reverse order
    16→
    17→---
    18→
    19→## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl: The Network Filter Entry Point
    20→
    21→### Location
    22→- Header: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h`
    23→- Implementation: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`
    24→
    25→### Responsibilities
    26→
    27→**ConnectionManagerImpl** is the primary entry point for HTTP request processing. It is a `Network::ReadFilter` that lives on each downstream TCP connection and orchestrates the entire request lifecycle.
    28→
    29→#### 1.1 Connection-Level Ownership
    30→
    31→```cpp
    32→class ConnectionManagerImpl : public Network::Re

Perfect! I've successfully created a comprehensive architecture document for Envoy's HTTP Connection Manager. Here's what I've delivered:

## Document Summary

**Location**: `/workspace/documentation.md`

The document covers the four major HCM components and their interactions:

### 1. **ConnectionManagerImpl** (The Entry Point)
- How it implements `Network::ReadFilter` to receive raw bytes
- Lazy codec creation for H1/H2/H3
- `ActiveStream` creation and management per request
- Connection-level concerns (watermarks, drain decisions, overload protection)

### 2. **FilterManager** (Per-Stream Filter Chain)
- Decoder filter chain execution (forward iteration: A→B→C)
- Encoder filter chain execution (reverse iteration: C→B→A)
- `ActiveStreamFilterBase` wrapper for managing filter state
- Filter stopping, buffering, and resumption mechanisms
- Local reply handling and error management

### 3. **Router Filter** (Upstream Dispatcher)
- Route selection via `RouteConfiguration` matching
- Cluster resolution and host selection
- Connection pool acquisition and load balancing
- `UpstreamRequest` lifecycle for managing upstream communication
- Retry logic, timeout handling, shadow routing

### 4. **ClusterManager & Upstream Connectivity**
- `ThreadLocalCluster` as the thread-safe cluster interface
- Connection pool architecture (idle connection reuse, circuit breakers)
- Load balancing algorithms (round-robin, consistent hash, subset LB, etc.)
- Health checking and outlier detection
- xDS cluster configuration updates

### Key Features Included:

✅ **Component responsibilities** - What each part owns  
✅ **Data flow diagrams** - Request and response paths with detailed step-by-step flow  
✅ **Extension points** - HTTP filters, route configuration, cluster extensions, codecs, acces

19. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is Envoy's core subsystem for processing HTTP requests from downstream clients, transforming them according to configured routing and filtering rules, and forwarding them to upstream services. This document explains the design and interactions between the four major components that implement this functionality.\n\nThe HCM request processing pipeline follows this flow:\n1. **Raw bytes arrive** on a downstream TCP connection\n2. **ConnectionManagerImpl** (Network::ReadFilter) receives and decodes them\n3. **ActiveStream** is created per request and manages per-stream state\n4. **FilterManager** executes the configured HTTP filter chain\n5. **Router Filter** (terminal decoder filter) performs route selection and upstream forwarding\n6. **UpstreamRequest** manages the upstream connection and stream lifecycle\n7. **ClusterManager** and **ThreadLocalCluster** provide connection pools to upstream services\n8. **Responses flow back** through the filter chain in reverse order\n\n---\n\n## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl: The Network Filter Entry Point\n\n### Location\n- Header: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h`\n- Implementation: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n**ConnectionManagerImpl** is the primary entry point for HTTP request processing. It is a `Network::ReadFilter` that lives on each downstream TCP connection and orchestrates the entire request lifecycle.\n\n#### 1.1 Connection-Level Ownership\n\n```cpp\nclass ConnectionManagerImpl : public Network::ReadFilter,\n                             public ServerConnectionCallbacks,\n                             public Network::ConnectionCallbacks,\n                             public Http::ApiListener\n```\n\nThe class serves multiple roles:\n- **Network::ReadFilter**: Receives raw socket data via `onData()` and `onNewConnection()`\n- **ServerConnectionCallbacks**: Implements codec callbacks for new streams (`newStream()`)\n- **Network::ConnectionCallbacks**: Handles connection events (close, drain)\n- **Http::ApiListener**: Supports API-driven request injection\n\n#### 1.2 Lazy Codec Creation\n\nHTTP codecs (H1, H2, H3) are created on-demand:\n- **H3 (QUIC)**: Created in `onNewConnection()`\n- **H1/H2**: Created in `onData()` when the first bytes arrive\n- **API Listener mode**: Created via explicit `createCodec()` call\n\nThe codec interprets raw bytes and signals stream creation through `ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream()`.\n\n#### 1.3 ActiveStream Management\n\nWhen a new HTTP stream arrives, the codec calls `newStream()` to create an **ActiveStream**, which wraps a single request/response pair:\n\n```cpp\nstruct ActiveStream : public LinkedObject<ActiveStream>,\n                      public Event::DeferredDeletable,\n                      public StreamCallbacks,\n                      public CodecEventCallbacks,\n                      public RequestDecoder,\n                      public Tracing::Config,\n                      public FilterManagerCallbacks,\n                      public DownstreamStreamFilterCallbacks,\n                      public RouteCache\n```\n\nEach **ActiveStream**:\n- Holds the HTTP codec's `ResponseEncoder` for sending responses downstream\n- Contains a `FilterManager` instance that executes the filter chain\n- Manages stream-level state: headers, trailers, metadata, body data\n- Implements request decoder interface for receiving codec events\n- Acts as `FilterManagerCallbacks` to receive filter-produced output (headers, data, trailers)\n- Implements `DownstreamStreamFilterCallbacks` for filter-to-HCM signaling (route updates, timeouts)\n\n#### 1.4 Connection-Level Concerns\n\n**Flow Control (Watermarks)**:\n- The HTTP codec signals watermark events (`onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()`, `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()`) when the underlying TCP write buffer is full/empty\n- ConnectionManagerImpl propagates these to all active streams\n- Streams use watermarks to signal back-pressure to upstream hosts\n\n**Drain Management**:\n- ConnectionManagerImpl monitors the `Network::DrainDecision` to detect when the server is draining\n- During drain, no new HTTP/2 streams are accepted on the connection (HTTP/1.1 connections complete in-flight requests then close)\n\n**Overload Protection**:\n- Integrates with `Server::OverloadManager` to detect resource exhaustion\n- Can stop accepting new streams or close connections when overloaded\n- Tracks premature stream resets and can drain connections based on reset ratios\n\n#### 1.5 Codec Selection Architecture\n\nThe codec is selected lazily based on the first data received. This is important because:\n- The protocol might not be known until bytes arrive (except for H3 where QUIC's stream setup provides the info)\n- Different protocols have different multiplexing and streaming semantics\n- The codec drives all downstream behavior through callback interfaces\n\n---\n\n## 2. FilterManager: The Per-Stream Filter Chain Execution Engine\n\n### Location\n- Header: `source/common/http/filter_manager.h`\n- Implementation: `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n**FilterManager** is responsible for:\n1. Creating filters via `FilterChainFactory`\n2. Executing the decoder filter chain (request processing)\n3. Managing filter state and iteration\n4. Executing the encoder filter chain (response processing)\n5. Handling local replies and stream reset logic\n\n### 2.1 The Filter Chain Architecture\n\nThe FilterManager maintains two filter chains:\n\n#### Decoder Filter Chain (Request Path)\n\n```cpp\nstruct StreamDecoderFilters {\n  using Element = ActiveStreamDecoderFilter;\n  using Iterator = std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr>::iterator;\n\n  Iterator begin() { return entries_.begin(); }\n  Iterator end() { return entries_.end(); }\n\n  std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n};\n```\n\n**Iteration order**: Filters are iterated **forward** (A, B, C, ...) as configured.\n\n**Filter types participating**:\n- `StreamDecoderFilter`: Processes request (decode headers, data, trailers)\n- `StreamFilter`: Dual-mode filter (both decoder and encoder)\n\n**Execution flow**:\n1. Codec calls `decodeHeaders()` on ActiveStream\n2. ActiveStream delegates to FilterManager: `decodeHeaders()`\n3. FilterManager iterates through decoder filters, calling each filter's `decodeHeaders()`\n4. Filter returns `FilterHeadersStatus`:\n   - `Continue`: Move to next filter\n   - `StopIteration`: Pause (other filters don't process these headers yet)\n   - `StopAllIteration`: Buffer subsequent data until resumed\n5. Repeat for `decodeData()` and `decodeTrailers()`\n\n#### Encoder Filter Chain (Response Path)\n\n```cpp\nstruct StreamEncoderFilters {\n  using Element = ActiveStreamEncoderFilter;\n  using Iterator = std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr>::reverse_iterator;\n\n  Iterator begin() { return entries_.rbegin(); }\n  Iterator end() { return entries_.rend(); }\n\n  std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n};\n```\n\n**Iteration order**: Filters are iterated in **reverse** (C, B, A, ...) as configured.\n\n**Rationale**: Responses flow back through the filter stack in reverse order, allowing each filter to \"unwrap\" the request processing (last-in-first-out).\n\n### 2.2 The ActiveStreamFilterBase Wrapper\n\nEvery filter (decoder or encoder) is wrapped in an `ActiveStreamFilterBase`:\n\n```cpp\nstruct ActiveStreamFilterBase : public StreamFilterCallbacks,\n                               Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::http> {\n  ActiveStreamFilterBase(FilterManager& parent, absl::string_view filter_config_name)\n      : parent_(filter), iteration_state_(IterationState::Continue) {}\n\n  // Called after filter callbacks to handle iteration state changes\n  bool commonHandleAfterHeadersCallback(FilterHeadersStatus status, bool& end_stream);\n  bool commonHandleAfterDataCallback(FilterDataStatus status, Buffer::Instance& data,\n                                     bool& buffer_was_streaming);\n  // ... other callbacks\n```\n\nThe wrapper:\n- Holds the iteration state (Continue, StopSingleIteration, StopAllBuffer, StopAllWatermark)\n- Buffers data when iteration is paused\n- Calls the filter's callback methods and interprets return statuses\n- Updates iteration state and resumes other filters when the filter signals readiness\n\n### 2.3 Filter Stopping and Resumption\n\nWhen a filter returns `StopIteration` or `StopAllIteration`:\n- Downstream filters in the chain don't process the current headers/data/trailers\n- The filter can inspect/modify the data and call `continueIteration()` to resume\n\nWhen `StopAllIteration` is returned:\n- Subsequent data is **buffered** until the filter resumes\n- If the buffer exceeds the limit or reaches a watermark, back-pressure is applied to the upstream\n\n### 2.4 Local Replies and Error Handling\n\n**DownstreamFilterManager** (the concrete decoder-side FilterManager) handles local replies:\n- Filter or other component calls `sendLocalReply(Code, body, headers_callback, ...)`\n- FilterManager encodes the response headers and body directly to the codec\n- Skips remaining decoder filters and goes directly to encoder filters for response processing\n\n**Common local reply scenarios**:\n- Codec errors (invalid headers): 400 Bad Request\n- Timeout (router filter timeout): 504 Gateway Timeout\n- No healthy upstream: 503 Service Unavailable\n- Filter logic errors: varies by filter\n\n---\n\n## 3. Router Filter: The Terminal Decoder Filter and Upstream Dispatcher\n\n### Location\n- Header: `source/common/router/router.h`\n- Implementation: `source/common/router/router.cc`\n- Config: `source/extensions/filters/http/router/config.cc`\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nThe Router Filter is:\n1. A `StreamDecoderFilter` (part of the decoder chain, typically terminal/last)\n2. The upstream request dispatcher\n3. The route selector and cluster loader\n\n### 3.1 Route Selection\n\nWhen `decodeHeaders()` is called:\n\n```cpp\nHttp::FilterHeadersStatus Filter::decodeHeaders(Http::RequestHeaderMap& headers,\n                                                bool end_stream) override;\n```\n\nThe router:\n1. **Selects the route**: Uses the request headers and connection properties to query the `RouteConfiguration` and find a matching `RouteEntry`\n2. **Resolves the cluster**: Extracts the cluster name from the route entry\n3. **Calls continueDecodeHeaders()** to finalize upstream request setup:\n   ```cpp\n   bool continueDecodeHeaders(Upstream::ThreadLocalCluster* cluster,\n                              Http::RequestHeaderMap& headers,\n                              bool end_stream, Upstream::HostConstSharedPtr&& host,\n                              absl::string_view host_selection_details = {});\n   ```\n\n### 3.2 Route vs. Cluster Resolution\n\n**Route Selection** uses the `Router::RouteConfiguration`:\n- Matches virtual hosts by domain/SNI\n- Matches routes within a virtual host by path, method, headers, etc.\n- Returns a `RouteEntry` with metadata:\n  - Cluster name\n  - Timeout policy\n  - Retry policy\n  - Shadow policy\n  - Request/response header modifications\n  - Per-route filter config\n\n**Cluster Lookup** in `continueDecodeHeaders()`:\n```cpp\nUpstream::ThreadLocalCluster* cluster = clusterManager().getThreadLocalCluster(cluster_name);\n```\n- Gets a reference to the thread-local cluster wrapper\n- Used to obtain connection pools and load balance to hosts\n\n### 3.3 Host Selection and Connection Pool Acquisition\n\nThe router uses Envoy's **load balancer context** to select a host:\n\n```cpp\nclass Filter : public Upstream::LoadBalancerContextBase { ... };\n```\n\nWithin the LoadBalancerContext:\n- **computeHashKey()**: Returns hash for consistent hashing policies\n- **metadataMatchCriteria()**: Returns endpoint metadata for subset load balancing\n- Other LB context info (request headers, routing metadata)\n\nThe cluster's load balancer is called:\n```cpp\nUpstream::HostConstSharedPtr host = cluster->loadBalancer().chooseHost(&filter);\n```\n\nThis returns a specific `Host` (upstream endpoint).\n\nOnce a host is selected, the router creates an **UpstreamRequest**:\n```cpp\nupstream_requests_.push_back(std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(..., conn_pool, ...));\n```\n\nWhere the `conn_pool` is obtained from:\n```cpp\nHttp::ConnectionPool::InstancePtr pool =\n    cluster->httpConnPool(host, ResourcePriority, protocol, &context);\n```\n\n### 3.4 Upstream Request Lifecycle: UpstreamRequest\n\n**UpstreamRequest** (defined in `source/common/router/upstream_request.h`) represents the router's interaction with a single upstream host.\n\n#### Key responsibilities:\n1. **Request forwarding**: Accepts headers/data/trailers from the router filter and forwards them to the upstream via the connection pool\n2. **Response reception**: Receives response headers/data/trailers from the upstream and calls back to the router filter\n3. **Retry management**: On failures, the router can create a new UpstreamRequest to retry\n4. **Timeout handling**: Per-try timeouts and global request timeouts\n5. **Filter chain management**: Manages the upstream filter manager\n\n**Initialization**:\n```cpp\nUpstreamRequest(RouterFilterInterface& parent, std::unique_ptr<GenericConnPool>&& conn_pool,\n                bool can_send_early_data, bool can_use_http3, bool enable_half_close);\n```\n\nThe UpstreamRequest registers itself as a `GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks`:\n```cpp\nvirtual void onPoolReady(std::unique_ptr<GenericUpstream>&& upstream,\n                         Upstream::HostDescriptionConstSharedPtr host,\n                         const Network::ConnectionInfoProvider& address_provider,\n                         StreamInfo::StreamInfo& info, absl::optional<Http::Protocol> protocol);\n\nvirtual void onPoolFailure(ConnectionPool::PoolFailureReason reason,\n                           absl::string_view transport_failure_reason,\n                           Upstream::HostDescriptionConstSharedPtr host);\n```\n\n**Request forwarding**:\n```cpp\nvirtual void acceptHeadersFromRouter(bool end_stream);\nvirtual void acceptDataFromRouter(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream);\nvoid acceptTrailersFromRouter(Http::RequestTrailerMap& trailers);\n```\n\nThese methods:\n1. Pass headers/data/trailers through the upstream filter manager\n2. The upstream filter manager's terminal filter (UpstreamCodecFilter) encodes to the upstream codec\n3. Data is sent on the upstream connection\n\n**Response processing**:\nWhen the upstream codec produces response data, the UpstreamCodecFilter calls the UpstreamRequest's decoder methods:\n```cpp\nvoid decodeHeaders(Http::ResponseHeaderMapPtr&& headers, bool end_stream);\nvoid decodeData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream);\nvoid decodeTrailers(Http::ResponseTrailerMapPtr&& trailers);\n```\n\nThese are passed through the upstream filter manager (in reverse order) and eventually routed back to the router filter's `onUpstreamHeaders()`, `onUpstreamData()`, etc.\n\n### 3.5 Retry Logic\n\nOn upstream failure (connection failure, stream reset, 5xx response), the router filter can:\n1. Check the route's retry policy\n2. If retries remain, create a new UpstreamRequest to a different host\n3. Forward the same request headers/data again\n\nThe retry state is tracked in the filter and manages:\n- Retry budget (how many retries are allowed)\n- Per-try timeout vs. global timeout\n- Hosts that have already been attempted\n\n### 3.6 Shadow Routing and Hedged Requests\n\n**Shadow Routing**:\n- The route entry specifies a shadow cluster\n- The router filter creates a secondary UpstreamRequest to the shadow cluster\n- Shadow traffic uses the same request but responses are discarded\n- No client impact (shadow failures don't affect the primary response)\n\n**Request Hedging** (advanced feature):\n- On per-try timeout, before the global timeout expires, create a second UpstreamRequest\n- Both requests proceed in parallel\n- Return the first successful response to the client\n\n---\n\n## 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity\n\n### Location\n- Interface: `envoy/upstream/cluster_manager.h`\n- Implementation: `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.cc`\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nThe **ClusterManager** is the persistent, server-wide component that manages:\n1. Cluster configurations (static and dynamic)\n2. Per-cluster thread-local state (connection pools, load balancers)\n3. Host health checking and outlier detection\n4. xDS subscription and cluster updates\n\n### 4.1 ThreadLocalCluster: The Thread-Safe Cluster Interface\n\nThe router gets clusters via:\n```cpp\nUpstream::ThreadLocalCluster* cluster =\n    clusterManager().getThreadLocalCluster(cluster_name);\n```\n\n**ThreadLocalCluster** is a thread-local wrapper that provides:\n1. **Host selection**: `chooseHost(LoadBalancerContext*)`\n2. **Connection pool access**:\n   ```cpp\n   Http::ConnectionPool::InstancePtr httpConnPool(\n       Upstream::HostConstSharedPtr,\n       ResourcePriority,\n       absl::optional<Http::Protocol>,\n       Http::LoadBalancerContext*);\n   ```\n3. **Cluster info**: `info()` returns the `Upstream::ClusterInfo` (name, protocol, TLS config, etc.)\n\nThe ThreadLocalCluster is thread-safe because each thread has its own instance in a thread-local slot. This avoids lock contention on per-thread data like connection pools.\n\n### 4.2 Connection Pool Architecture\n\n**HttpConnPool** (or **TcpConnPool** for non-HTTP protocols) is the component that:\n1. **Maintains idle connections**: Keep-alive connections to upstream hosts\n2. **Creates new connections**: When idle pools are exhausted\n3. **Limits concurrency**: Enforces circuit breaker settings\n4. **Routes requests**: Distributes requests across connections\n\n**Interface for acquiring a stream**:\n```cpp\nclass ConnectionPool::Instance {\n  virtual Cancellable* newStream(StreamCallbacks& callbacks) = 0;\n};\n```\n\nWhen the router's UpstreamRequest calls `pool->newStream(callbacks)`:\n1. If an idle connection exists, it's immediately reused\n2. If no idle connection, a new one is created (connection pool owns the TCP connection)\n3. The pool owns the HTTP codec for that connection\n4. The pool calls `callbacks->onPoolReady(upstream)` when ready to send\n\n**Connection limits**:\nThe connection pool is configured with:\n- `max_connections`: Total concurrent connections to a host\n- `max_pending_requests`: Queue depth when no connections are available\n- `max_requests_per_connection`: How many requests per H2 connection (or always 1 for H1)\n\n### 4.3 Load Balancing: Cluster \u2192 Host Selection\n\n**Load Balancing** happens in two stages:\n\n**Stage 1: Cluster selection** (by router via route configuration)\n- Which cluster should handle this request?\n- Determined by the route entry\n\n**Stage 2: Host selection** (within the selected cluster)\n- Which endpoint in the cluster should receive the connection?\n- Determined by the cluster's **LoadBalancer**\n\nThe LoadBalancer implements various algorithms:\n- **Round-robin**: Cycle through healthy hosts\n- **Least request**: Pick the host with fewest active requests\n- **Consistent hash**: Same request properties \u2192 same host (for session persistence)\n- **Ring hash** / **Maglev**: Advanced consistent hashing\n- **Subset LB**: Filter hosts by metadata, then apply LB algorithm\n- **Locality-aware**: Prefer hosts in the same zone/region\n\nThe router passes a `LoadBalancerContext` (implemented by the Filter itself) to provide:\n- Request headers (for header-based routing or hashing)\n- Metadata match criteria (for subset LB)\n- Cookie information (for hash-based routing)\n\n### 4.4 Health Checking and Outlier Detection\n\n**Health Checking**:\n- Each cluster can have active health checkers configured\n- Periodic checks (HTTP requests or TCP connections) to endpoints\n- Unhealthy endpoints are removed from the load balancer's pool\n\n**Outlier Detection** (passive health checking):\n- If an endpoint sees too many failures, it's temporarily marked unhealthy\n- After a recovery period with successful requests, it's re-enabled\n- Reduces cascading failures by temporarily removing bad endpoints\n\nThe load balancer's **host set** is updated when health status changes. The next time `chooseHost()` is called, unhealthy hosts are skipped.\n\n### 4.5 Cluster Configuration Updates (xDS)\n\nClusterManager subscribes to CDS (Cluster Discovery Service) for dynamic cluster updates:\n- New clusters are added\n- Existing clusters are updated (e.g., endpoint changes, circuit breaker settings)\n- Clusters are removed\n\nWhen a cluster is updated:\n1. ClusterManager creates/updates the in-memory cluster representation\n2. Cluster warming happens (health checks initialize, etc.)\n3. Once warmed, the cluster is made available to workers via ThreadLocalCluster\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: An HTTP Request Through the HCM\n\n### Downstream Request Path\n\n```\n1. TCP Data Arrives\n   \u2193\n2. ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()\n   \u2514\u2500 Codec decodes bytes\n   \u2514\u2500 Codec calls ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream()\n\n3. ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream() creates ActiveStream\n   \u2514\u2500 ActiveStream creates FilterManager\n   \u2514\u2500 FilterManager creates filters (via FilterChainFactory)\n\n4. Codec calls ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()\n   \u2193\n5. ActiveStream::decodeHeaders() \u2192 FilterManager::decodeHeaders()\n   \u2193\n6. FilterManager iterates decoder filters:\n   Filter[0]::decodeHeaders() \u2192 Filter[1]::decodeHeaders() \u2192 ... \u2192 Router Filter::decodeHeaders()\n\n7. Router Filter:\n   \u251c\u2500 Selects route from RouteConfiguration\n   \u251c\u2500 Resolves cluster name\n   \u251c\u2500 Gets ThreadLocalCluster from ClusterManager\n   \u251c\u2500 Calls LoadBalancer::chooseHost() \u2192 selects endpoint\n   \u251c\u2500 Requests connection pool from cluster: cluster->httpConnPool()\n   \u2514\u2500 Creates UpstreamRequest(conn_pool)\n\n8. UpstreamRequest registers as pool callbacks:\n   \u2514\u2500 Waits for onPoolReady() or onPoolFailure()\n\n9. Connection pool processing:\n   \u251c\u2500 If idle connection available: call onPoolReady() immediately\n   \u251c\u2500 If no idle connection:\n   \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Create new TCP connection (if under max_connections)\n   \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Initialize HTTP codec\n   \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Call onPoolReady(upstream)\n   \u2514\u2500 If max connections reached: queue in pending list\n\n10. UpstreamRequest::onPoolReady():\n    \u251c\u2500 Registers for upstream codec events\n    \u251c\u2500 Creates upstream filter manager\n    \u251c\u2500 Calls acceptHeadersFromRouter()\n    \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Passes headers through upstream filter manager\n    \u2502  \u2514\u2500 UpstreamCodecFilter encodes to upstream codec\n    \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Data sent on upstream TCP connection\n    \u2514\u2500 Waits for response\n\n11. Codec processes body data:\n    Codec \u2192 ActiveStream::decodeData() \u2192 FilterManager::decodeData()\n    \u2192 (decoder filters process, may buffer/modify/stop)\n    \u2192 Router Filter::decodeData() \u2192 UpstreamRequest::acceptDataFromRouter()\n    \u2192 (upstream filters) \u2192 UpstreamCodecFilter \u2192 upstream codec \u2192 wire\n```\n\n### Upstream Response Path\n\n```\n1. Upstream server sends response\n   \u2193\n2. Upstream TCP connection receives data\n   \u2514\u2500 Upstream codec decodes bytes\n   \u2514\u2500 Upstream codec calls UpstreamCodecFilter callbacks\n\n3. UpstreamCodecFilter (terminal upstream filter) calls:\n   UpstreamRequest::decodeHeaders/Data/Trailers()\n   \u2193\n4. UpstreamRequest passes through upstream filter manager (reverse order)\n   \u2514\u2500 Filters can modify, buffer, or stop iteration\n   \u2193\n5. UpstreamRequest signals back to Router Filter:\n   onUpstreamHeaders() \u2192 onUpstreamData() \u2192 onUpstreamTrailers()\n   \u2193\n6. Router Filter calls FilterManager to encode response:\n   Filter1::encodeHeaders() \u2190 Filter2::encodeHeaders() \u2190 ... \u2190 Router\n   (Note: encoder chain is reversed)\n   \u2193\n7. FilterManager sends encoded response downstream:\n   ActiveStream::encodeHeaders() \u2192 Codec::encodeHeaders()\n   \u2193\n8. Codec sends response bytes on downstream TCP connection\n   \u2193\n9. Client receives response\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\nEnvoy's HCM provides several mechanisms for customization:\n\n### 1. HTTP Filters\n\nFilters are the primary extension mechanism. They can:\n- **Decoder filters**: Inspect/modify requests, add request headers, stop iteration\n- **Encoder filters**: Inspect/modify responses, add response headers\n- **Terminal filters**: Make forwarding decisions (Router filter is an example)\n\nFilter types:\n```cpp\n// Decoder-only\nclass StreamDecoderFilter { ... };\n\n// Encoder-only\nclass StreamEncoderFilter { ... };\n\n// Dual-mode (both decoder and encoder)\nclass StreamFilter : public StreamDecoderFilter, public StreamEncoderFilter { ... };\n```\n\nCommon filters:\n- **Router**: Forwards to upstream clusters\n- **Authentication (auth)**: Validates JWTs, OAuth tokens\n- **Rate limiting**: Enforces per-second request limits\n- **Buffer**: Buffers request body for inspection\n- **Lua**: Scripted request/response manipulation\n- **Access log**: Logs requests after completion\n- **Compression**: Compresses response body\n- **Header rewrite**: Adds/removes/modifies headers\n\n### 2. Route Configuration\n\nThe RouteConfiguration specifies:\n- Virtual hosts (domain matching)\n- Routes (path matching, method matching, header matching)\n- Per-route actions:\n  - Cluster name\n  - Timeout policy\n  - Retry policy\n  - Weighted clusters (load balancing across multiple clusters)\n  - Redirect rules\n  - Direct response (bypass upstream)\n  - Per-route filter config (enable/disable/configure filters)\n\n### 3. Cluster Extensions\n\nClusters are extensible:\n- **Load balancing policies**: Custom LB algorithms\n- **Connection pool factories**: Different protocol implementations (HTTP/1, HTTP/2, gRPC, etc.)\n- **Health checkers**: Active health check implementations\n- **Outlier detection**: Custom failure detection algorithms\n\n### 4. Codec Extensions\n\nNew HTTP protocol versions or variants can be plugged in:\n- HTTP/1.1: `source/common/http/http1/`\n- HTTP/2: `source/common/http/http2/`\n- HTTP/3 (QUIC): `source/common/http/http3/`\n\nEach implements the `Http::Connection` interface for codec creation and the `Http::CodecFactory` for instantiation.\n\n### 5. Access Logging\n\nAccess logs are specified in HCM configuration and filters:\n- Format string with variable substitution (request headers, response headers, response time, etc.)\n- Multiple log destinations (files, gRPC, etc.)\n- Filter expressions to conditionally log\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling and Recovery\n\n### Codec Errors\n\nIf the HTTP codec encounters invalid data (bad request line, malformed headers):\n1. Codec signals error via `StreamDecoderFilterCallbacks::sendLocalReply()`\n2. HCM generates a 400 Bad Request response\n3. Response is sent to client\n4. Connection may be closed (depending on protocol and error severity)\n\n### Filter Errors\n\nIf a filter encounters an error during processing:\n- Filter calls `sendLocalReply()` with appropriate error code\n- FilterManager stops executing further decoder filters\n- Response is sent downstream\n- Router filter is notified via `onLocalReply()` to clean up upstream resources\n\n### Upstream Connection Failures\n\nIf the connection pool fails to establish a connection:\n1. UpstreamRequest::onPoolFailure() is called with failure reason\n2. Router filter checks retry policy\n3. If retries available:\n   - Create new UpstreamRequest\n   - Attempt same headers/data on different host or cluster\n4. If no retries or all attempts fail:\n   - Router sends local reply (503 Service Unavailable)\n   - Response sent to client\n\n### Upstream Stream Resets\n\nIf the upstream stream resets mid-transmission:\n1. UpstreamRequest is notified\n2. Router filter is notified via onResetStream()\n3. Router checks if retry is possible\n4. If yes: create new UpstreamRequest and retry\n5. If no: reset downstream stream or send local reply\n\n### Timeout Handling\n\n**Per-try timeout**:\n- Set by UpstreamRequest when forwarding headers\n- If upstream doesn't respond within timeout, connection/stream is reset\n- Triggers retry if allowed\n\n**Global request timeout**:\n- Set by router filter based on route config\n- Applies to entire request (all retries combined)\n- If exceeded, downstream stream is reset with timeout error\n\n---\n\n## Performance Considerations\n\n### 1. Memory Efficiency\n\n- **ActiveStream pooling**: Streams are allocated on-demand and deferred-deleted to avoid allocation during busy periods\n- **Filter buffering**: Data is buffered in memory-aware buffers that track allocation\n- **Connection pooling**: Idle connections are kept in pools to avoid connection setup overhead\n\n### 2. Request Pipelining\n\n- **HTTP/1.1**: Requests are processed sequentially; pipelining is supported but requires careful ordering\n- **HTTP/2**: Multiple streams per connection are multiplexed at codec level\n- **Connection reuse**: Keep-alive connections reduce latency\n\n### 3. Watermarks and Backpressure\n\n- **Read watermarks**: When buffers fill, reading is disabled to prevent memory exhaustion\n- **Write watermarks**: When downstream write buffers fill, upstream reading is disabled\n- **Filter-level watermarks**: Filters can signal back-pressure when they can't process data\n\n### 4. Load Balancing Efficiency\n\n- **Sticky sessions**: Consistent hashing keeps client requests on same upstream\n- **Locality awareness**: Prefers nearby endpoints to reduce latency\n- **Connection multiplexing**: HTTP/2 multiplexing allows many requests per connection\n\n---\n\n## Key Source Files\n\n### Connection Management\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/cc`: ConnectionManagerImpl and ActiveStream\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_config.h`: Configuration interface\n\n### Filter Chain\n- `source/common/http/filter_manager.h/cc`: FilterManager, stream filter wrappers\n- `source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h`: Filter creation utilities\n- `envoy/http/filter.h`: Filter interface definitions\n\n### Routing\n- `source/common/router/router.h/cc`: Router filter implementation\n- `source/common/router/config_impl.h/cc`: Route configuration and matching\n- `source/common/router/upstream_request.h/cc`: UpstreamRequest lifecycle\n- `source/extensions/filters/http/router/config.cc`: Router filter factory\n\n### Cluster Management\n- `envoy/upstream/cluster_manager.h`: ClusterManager interface\n- `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h/cc`: ClusterManagerImpl\n- `source/common/upstream/cluster_impl.h/cc`: Cluster and host management\n- `source/common/upstream/load_balancer_impl.h/cc`: Load balancer algorithms\n\n### Codecs\n- `source/common/http/http1/codec_impl.h/cc`: HTTP/1.1 codec\n- `source/common/http/http2/codec_impl.h/cc`: HTTP/2 codec\n- `source/common/http/http3/`: HTTP/3 (QUIC) codec\n\n### Connection Pools\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h/cc`: HTTP connection pool base\n- `source/common/http/http1/conn_pool.h/cc`: HTTP/1.1 connection pool\n- `source/common/http/http2/conn_pool.h/cc`: HTTP/2 connection pool\n\n---\n\n## References\n\nThis document covers the core HCM architecture for HTTP request processing. For additional detail:\n\n1. **Dynamic Configuration (xDS)**: See CDS (Cluster Discovery Service) and RDS (Route Discovery Service) for how routes and clusters are updated at runtime\n2. **Tracing**: HCM integrates with OpenTelemetry/Jaeger for distributed tracing\n3. **Metrics**: HCM emits detailed metrics for requests, connections, upstream hosts\n4. **TLS/SSL**: HCM supports both downstream and upstream TLS with certificate management and validation\n5. **Virtual Hosts and Scoped Routes**: Advanced routing features for multi-tenancy and version management\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"

Output
{
  "content": "# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nThe HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is Envoy's core subsystem for processing HTTP requests from downstream clients, transforming them according to configured routing and filtering rules, and forwarding them to upstream services. This document explains the design and interactions between the four major components that implement this functionality.\n\nThe HCM request processing pipeline follows this flow:\n1. **Raw bytes arrive** on a downstream TCP connection\n2. **ConnectionManagerImpl** (Network::ReadFilter) receives and decodes them\n3. **ActiveStream** is created per request and manages per-stream state\n4. **FilterManager** executes the configured HTTP filter chain\n5. **Router Filter** (terminal decoder filter) performs route selection and upstream forwarding\n6. **UpstreamRequest** manages the upstream connection and stream lifecycle\n7. **ClusterManager** and **ThreadLocalCluster** provide connection pools to upstream services\n8. **Responses flow back** through the filter chain in reverse order\n\n---\n\n## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl: The Network Filter Entry Point\n\n### Location\n- Header: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h`\n- Implementation: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n**ConnectionManagerImpl** is the primary entry point for HTTP request processing. It is a `Network::ReadFilter` that lives on each downstream TCP connection and orchestrates the entire request lifecycle.\n\n#### 1.1 Connection-Level Ownership\n\n```cpp\nclass ConnectionManagerImpl : public Network::ReadFilter,\n                             public ServerConnectionCallbacks,\n                             public Network::ConnectionCallbacks,\n                             public Http::ApiListener\n```\n\nThe class serves multiple roles:\n- **Network::ReadFilter**: Receives raw socket data via `onData()` and `onNewConnection()`\n- **ServerConnectionCallbacks**: Implements codec callbacks for new streams (`newStream()`)\n- **Network::ConnectionCallbacks**: Handles connection events (close, drain)\n- **Http::ApiListener**: Supports API-driven request injection\n\n#### 1.2 Lazy Codec Creation\n\nHTTP codecs (H1, H2, H3) are created on-demand:\n- **H3 (QUIC)**: Created in `onNewConnection()`\n- **H1/H2**: Created in `onData()` when the first bytes arrive\n- **API Listener mode**: Created via explicit `createCodec()` call\n\nThe codec interprets raw bytes and signals stream creation through `ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream()`.\n\n#### 1.3 ActiveStream Management\n\nWhen a new HTTP stream arrives, the codec calls `newStream()` to create an **ActiveStream**, which wraps a single request/response pair:\n\n```cpp\nstruct ActiveStream : public LinkedObject<ActiveStream>,\n                      public Event::DeferredDeletable,\n                      public StreamCallbacks,\n                      public CodecEventCallbacks,\n                      public RequestDecoder,\n                      public Tracing::Config,\n                      public FilterManagerCallbacks,\n                      public DownstreamStreamFilterCallbacks,\n                      public RouteCache\n```\n\nEach **ActiveStream**:\n- Holds the HTTP codec's `ResponseEncoder` for sending responses downstream\n- Contains a `FilterManager` instance that executes the filter chain\n- Manages stream-level state: headers, trailers, metadata, body data\n- Implements request decoder interface for receiving codec events\n- Acts as `FilterManagerCallbacks` to receive filter-produced output (headers, data, trailers)\n- Implements `DownstreamStreamFilterCallbacks` for filter-to-HCM signaling (route updates, timeouts)\n\n#### 1.4 Connection-Level Concerns\n\n**Flow Control (Watermarks)**:\n- The HTTP codec signals watermark events (`onAboveWriteBufferHighWatermark()`, `onBelowWriteBufferLowWatermark()`) when the underlying TCP write buffer is full/empty\n- ConnectionManagerImpl propagates these to all active streams\n- Streams use watermarks to signal back-pressure to upstream hosts\n\n**Drain Management**:\n- ConnectionManagerImpl monitors the `Network::DrainDecision` to detect when the server is draining\n- During drain, no new HTTP/2 streams are accepted on the connection (HTTP/1.1 connections complete in-flight requests then close)\n\n**Overload Protection**:\n- Integrates with `Server::OverloadManager` to detect resource exhaustion\n- Can stop accepting new streams or close connections when overloaded\n- Tracks premature stream resets and can drain connections based on reset ratios\n\n#### 1.5 Codec Selection Architecture\n\nThe codec is selected lazily based on the first data received. This is important because:\n- The protocol might not be known until bytes arrive (except for H3 where QUIC's stream setup provides the info)\n- Different protocols have different multiplexing and streaming semantics\n- The codec drives all downstream behavior through callback interfaces\n\n---\n\n## 2. FilterManager: The Per-Stream Filter Chain Execution Engine\n\n### Location\n- Header: `source/common/http/filter_manager.h`\n- Implementation: `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`\n\n### Responsibilities\n\n**FilterManager** is responsible for:\n1. Creating filters via `FilterChainFactory`\n2. Executing the decoder filter chain (request processing)\n3. Managing filter state and iteration\n4. Executing the encoder filter chain (response processing)\n5. Handling local replies and stream reset logic\n\n### 2.1 The Filter Chain Architecture\n\nThe FilterManager maintains two filter chains:\n\n#### Decoder Filter Chain (Request Path)\n\n```cpp\nstruct StreamDecoderFilters {\n  using Element = ActiveStreamDecoderFilter;\n  using Iterator = std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr>::iterator;\n\n  Iterator begin() { return entries_.begin(); }\n  Iterator end() { return entries_.end(); }\n\n  std::vector<ActiveStreamDecoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n};\n```\n\n**Iteration order**: Filters are iterated **forward** (A, B, C, ...) as configured.\n\n**Filter types participating**:\n- `StreamDecoderFilter`: Processes request (decode headers, data, trailers)\n- `StreamFilter`: Dual-mode filter (both decoder and encoder)\n\n**Execution flow**:\n1. Codec calls `decodeHeaders()` on ActiveStream\n2. ActiveStream delegates to FilterManager: `decodeHeaders()`\n3. FilterManager iterates through decoder filters, calling each filter's `decodeHeaders()`\n4. Filter returns `FilterHeadersStatus`:\n   - `Continue`: Move to next filter\n   - `StopIteration`: Pause (other filters don't process these headers yet)\n   - `StopAllIteration`: Buffer subsequent data until resumed\n5. Repeat for `decodeData()` and `decodeTrailers()`\n\n#### Encoder Filter Chain (Response Path)\n\n```cpp\nstruct StreamEncoderFilters {\n  using Element = ActiveStreamEncoderFilter;\n  using Iterator = std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr>::reverse_iterator;\n\n  Iterator begin() { return entries_.rbegin(); }\n  Iterator end() { return entries_.rend(); }\n\n  std::vector<ActiveStreamEncoderFilterPtr> entries_;\n};\n```\n\n**Iteration order**: Filters are iterated in **reverse** (C, B, A, ...) as configured.\n\n**Rationale**: Responses flow back through the filter stack in reverse order, allowing each filter to \"unwrap\" the request processing (last-in-first-out).\n\n### 2.2 The ActiveStreamFilterBase Wrapper\n\nEvery filter (decoder or encoder) is wrapped in an `ActiveStreamFilterBase`:\n\n```cpp\nstruct ActiveStreamFilterBase : public StreamFilterCallbacks,\n                               Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::http> {\n  ActiveStreamFilterBase(FilterManager& parent, absl::string_view filter_config_name)\n      : parent_(filter), iteration_state_(IterationState::Continue) {}\n\n  // Called after filter callbacks to handle iteration state changes\n  bool commonHandleAfterHeadersCallback(FilterHeadersStatus status, bool& end_stream);\n  bool commonHandleAfterDataCallback(FilterDataStatus status, Buffer::Instance& data,\n                                     bool& buffer_was_streaming);\n  // ... other callbacks\n```\n\nThe wrapper:\n- Holds the iteration state (Continue, StopSingleIteration, StopAllBuffer, StopAllWatermark)\n- Buffers data when iteration is paused\n- Calls the filter's callback methods and interprets return statuses\n- Updates iteration state and resumes other filters when the filter signals readiness\n\n### 2.3 Filter Stopping and Resumption\n\nWhen a filter returns `StopIteration` or `StopAllIteration`:\n- Downstream filters in the chain don't process the current headers/data/trailers\n- The filter can inspect/modify the data and call `continueIteration()` to resume\n\nWhen `StopAllIteration` is returned:\n- Subsequent data is **buffered** until the filter resumes\n- If the buffer exceeds the limit or reaches a watermark, back-pressure is applied to the upstream\n\n### 2.4 Local Replies and Error Handling\n\n**DownstreamFilterManager** (the concrete decoder-side FilterManager) handles local replies:\n- Filter or other component calls `sendLocalReply(Code, body, headers_callback, ...)`\n- FilterManager encodes the response headers and body directly to the codec\n- Skips remaining decoder filters and goes directly to encoder filters for response processing\n\n**Common local reply scenarios**:\n- Codec errors (invalid headers): 400 Bad Request\n- Timeout (router filter timeout): 504 Gateway Timeout\n- No healthy upstream: 503 Service Unavailable\n- Filter logic errors: varies by filter\n\n---\n\n## 3. Router Filter: The Terminal Decoder Filter and Upstream Dispatcher\n\n### Location\n- Header: `source/common/router/router.h`\n- Implementation: `source/common/router/router.cc`\n- Config: `source/extensions/filters/http/router/config.cc`\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nThe Router Filter is:\n1. A `StreamDecoderFilter` (part of the decoder chain, typically terminal/last)\n2. The upstream request dispatcher\n3. The route selector and cluster loader\n\n### 3.1 Route Selection\n\nWhen `decodeHeaders()` is called:\n\n```cpp\nHttp::FilterHeadersStatus Filter::decodeHeaders(Http::RequestHeaderMap& headers,\n                                                bool end_stream) override;\n```\n\nThe router:\n1. **Selects the route**: Uses the request headers and connection properties to query the `RouteConfiguration` and find a matching `RouteEntry`\n2. **Resolves the cluster**: Extracts the cluster name from the route entry\n3. **Calls continueDecodeHeaders()** to finalize upstream request setup:\n   ```cpp\n   bool continueDecodeHeaders(Upstream::ThreadLocalCluster* cluster,\n                              Http::RequestHeaderMap& headers,\n                              bool end_stream, Upstream::HostConstSharedPtr&& host,\n                              absl::string_view host_selection_details = {});\n   ```\n\n### 3.2 Route vs. Cluster Resolution\n\n**Route Selection** uses the `Router::RouteConfiguration`:\n- Matches virtual hosts by domain/SNI\n- Matches routes within a virtual host by path, method, headers, etc.\n- Returns a `RouteEntry` with metadata:\n  - Cluster name\n  - Timeout policy\n  - Retry policy\n  - Shadow policy\n  - Request/response header modifications\n  - Per-route filter config\n\n**Cluster Lookup** in `continueDecodeHeaders()`:\n```cpp\nUpstream::ThreadLocalCluster* cluster = clusterManager().getThreadLocalCluster(cluster_name);\n```\n- Gets a reference to the thread-local cluster wrapper\n- Used to obtain connection pools and load balance to hosts\n\n### 3.3 Host Selection and Connection Pool Acquisition\n\nThe router uses Envoy's **load balancer context** to select a host:\n\n```cpp\nclass Filter : public Upstream::LoadBalancerContextBase { ... };\n```\n\nWithin the LoadBalancerContext:\n- **computeHashKey()**: Returns hash for consistent hashing policies\n- **metadataMatchCriteria()**: Returns endpoint metadata for subset load balancing\n- Other LB context info (request headers, routing metadata)\n\nThe cluster's load balancer is called:\n```cpp\nUpstream::HostConstSharedPtr host = cluster->loadBalancer().chooseHost(&filter);\n```\n\nThis returns a specific `Host` (upstream endpoint).\n\nOnce a host is selected, the router creates an **UpstreamRequest**:\n```cpp\nupstream_requests_.push_back(std::make_unique<UpstreamRequest>(..., conn_pool, ...));\n```\n\nWhere the `conn_pool` is obtained from:\n```cpp\nHttp::ConnectionPool::InstancePtr pool =\n    cluster->httpConnPool(host, ResourcePriority, protocol, &context);\n```\n\n### 3.4 Upstream Request Lifecycle: UpstreamRequest\n\n**UpstreamRequest** (defined in `source/common/router/upstream_request.h`) represents the router's interaction with a single upstream host.\n\n#### Key responsibilities:\n1. **Request forwarding**: Accepts headers/data/trailers from the router filter and forwards them to the upstream via the connection pool\n2. **Response reception**: Receives response headers/data/trailers from the upstream and calls back to the router filter\n3. **Retry management**: On failures, the router can create a new UpstreamRequest to retry\n4. **Timeout handling**: Per-try timeouts and global request timeouts\n5. **Filter chain management**: Manages the upstream filter manager\n\n**Initialization**:\n```cpp\nUpstreamRequest(RouterFilterInterface& parent, std::unique_ptr<GenericConnPool>&& conn_pool,\n                bool can_send_early_data, bool can_use_http3, bool enable_half_close);\n```\n\nThe UpstreamRequest registers itself as a `GenericConnectionPoolCallbacks`:\n```cpp\nvirtual void onPoolReady(std::unique_ptr<GenericUpstream>&& upstream,\n                         Upstream::HostDescriptionConstSharedPtr host,\n                         const Network::ConnectionInfoProvider& address_provider,\n                         StreamInfo::StreamInfo& info, absl::optional<Http::Protocol> protocol);\n\nvirtual void onPoolFailure(ConnectionPool::PoolFailureReason reason,\n                           absl::string_view transport_failure_reason,\n                           Upstream::HostDescriptionConstSharedPtr host);\n```\n\n**Request forwarding**:\n```cpp\nvirtual void acceptHeadersFromRouter(bool end_stream);\nvirtual void acceptDataFromRouter(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream);\nvoid acceptTrailersFromRouter(Http::RequestTrailerMap& trailers);\n```\n\nThese methods:\n1. Pass headers/data/trailers through the upstream filter manager\n2. The upstream filter manager's terminal filter (UpstreamCodecFilter) encodes to the upstream codec\n3. Data is sent on the upstream connection\n\n**Response processing**:\nWhen the upstream codec produces response data, the UpstreamCodecFilter calls the UpstreamRequest's decoder methods:\n```cpp\nvoid decodeHeaders(Http::ResponseHeaderMapPtr&& headers, bool end_stream);\nvoid decodeData(Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream);\nvoid decodeTrailers(Http::ResponseTrailerMapPtr&& trailers);\n```\n\nThese are passed through the upstream filter manager (in reverse order) and eventually routed back to the router filter's `onUpstreamHeaders()`, `onUpstreamData()`, etc.\n\n### 3.5 Retry Logic\n\nOn upstream failure (connection failure, stream reset, 5xx response), the router filter can:\n1. Check the route's retry policy\n2. If retries remain, create a new UpstreamRequest to a different host\n3. Forward the same request headers/data again\n\nThe retry state is tracked in the filter and manages:\n- Retry budget (how many retries are allowed)\n- Per-try timeout vs. global timeout\n- Hosts that have already been attempted\n\n### 3.6 Shadow Routing and Hedged Requests\n\n**Shadow Routing**:\n- The route entry specifies a shadow cluster\n- The router filter creates a secondary UpstreamRequest to the shadow cluster\n- Shadow traffic uses the same request but responses are discarded\n- No client impact (shadow failures don't affect the primary response)\n\n**Request Hedging** (advanced feature):\n- On per-try timeout, before the global timeout expires, create a second UpstreamRequest\n- Both requests proceed in parallel\n- Return the first successful response to the client\n\n---\n\n## 4. Cluster Manager and Upstream Connectivity\n\n### Location\n- Interface: `envoy/upstream/cluster_manager.h`\n- Implementation: `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.cc`\n\n### Responsibilities\n\nThe **ClusterManager** is the persistent, server-wide component that manages:\n1. Cluster configurations (static and dynamic)\n2. Per-cluster thread-local state (connection pools, load balancers)\n3. Host health checking and outlier detection\n4. xDS subscription and cluster updates\n\n### 4.1 ThreadLocalCluster: The Thread-Safe Cluster Interface\n\nThe router gets clusters via:\n```cpp\nUpstream::ThreadLocalCluster* cluster =\n    clusterManager().getThreadLocalCluster(cluster_name);\n```\n\n**ThreadLocalCluster** is a thread-local wrapper that provides:\n1. **Host selection**: `chooseHost(LoadBalancerContext*)`\n2. **Connection pool access**:\n   ```cpp\n   Http::ConnectionPool::InstancePtr httpConnPool(\n       Upstream::HostConstSharedPtr,\n       ResourcePriority,\n       absl::optional<Http::Protocol>,\n       Http::LoadBalancerContext*);\n   ```\n3. **Cluster info**: `info()` returns the `Upstream::ClusterInfo` (name, protocol, TLS config, etc.)\n\nThe ThreadLocalCluster is thread-safe because each thread has its own instance in a thread-local slot. This avoids lock contention on per-thread data like connection pools.\n\n### 4.2 Connection Pool Architecture\n\n**HttpConnPool** (or **TcpConnPool** for non-HTTP protocols) is the component that:\n1. **Maintains idle connections**: Keep-alive connections to upstream hosts\n2. **Creates new connections**: When idle pools are exhausted\n3. **Limits concurrency**: Enforces circuit breaker settings\n4. **Routes requests**: Distributes requests across connections\n\n**Interface for acquiring a stream**:\n```cpp\nclass ConnectionPool::Instance {\n  virtual Cancellable* newStream(StreamCallbacks& callbacks) = 0;\n};\n```\n\nWhen the router's UpstreamRequest calls `pool->newStream(callbacks)`:\n1. If an idle connection exists, it's immediately reused\n2. If no idle connection, a new one is created (connection pool owns the TCP connection)\n3. The pool owns the HTTP codec for that connection\n4. The pool calls `callbacks->onPoolReady(upstream)` when ready to send\n\n**Connection limits**:\nThe connection pool is configured with:\n- `max_connections`: Total concurrent connections to a host\n- `max_pending_requests`: Queue depth when no connections are available\n- `max_requests_per_connection`: How many requests per H2 connection (or always 1 for H1)\n\n### 4.3 Load Balancing: Cluster \u2192 Host Selection\n\n**Load Balancing** happens in two stages:\n\n**Stage 1: Cluster selection** (by router via route configuration)\n- Which cluster should handle this request?\n- Determined by the route entry\n\n**Stage 2: Host selection** (within the selected cluster)\n- Which endpoint in the cluster should receive the connection?\n- Determined by the cluster's **LoadBalancer**\n\nThe LoadBalancer implements various algorithms:\n- **Round-robin**: Cycle through healthy hosts\n- **Least request**: Pick the host with fewest active requests\n- **Consistent hash**: Same request properties \u2192 same host (for session persistence)\n- **Ring hash** / **Maglev**: Advanced consistent hashing\n- **Subset LB**: Filter hosts by metadata, then apply LB algorithm\n- **Locality-aware**: Prefer hosts in the same zone/region\n\nThe router passes a `LoadBalancerContext` (implemented by the Filter itself) to provide:\n- Request headers (for header-based routing or hashing)\n- Metadata match criteria (for subset LB)\n- Cookie information (for hash-based routing)\n\n### 4.4 Health Checking and Outlier Detection\n\n**Health Checking**:\n- Each cluster can have active health checkers configured\n- Periodic checks (HTTP requests or TCP connections) to endpoints\n- Unhealthy endpoints are removed from the load balancer's pool\n\n**Outlier Detection** (passive health checking):\n- If an endpoint sees too many failures, it's temporarily marked unhealthy\n- After a recovery period with successful requests, it's re-enabled\n- Reduces cascading failures by temporarily removing bad endpoints\n\nThe load balancer's **host set** is updated when health status changes. The next time `chooseHost()` is called, unhealthy hosts are skipped.\n\n### 4.5 Cluster Configuration Updates (xDS)\n\nClusterManager subscribes to CDS (Cluster Discovery Service) for dynamic cluster updates:\n- New clusters are added\n- Existing clusters are updated (e.g., endpoint changes, circuit breaker settings)\n- Clusters are removed\n\nWhen a cluster is updated:\n1. ClusterManager creates/updates the in-memory cluster representation\n2. Cluster warming happens (health checks initialize, etc.)\n3. Once warmed, the cluster is made available to workers via ThreadLocalCluster\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: An HTTP Request Through the HCM\n\n### Downstream Request Path\n\n```\n1. TCP Data Arrives\n   \u2193\n2. ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()\n   \u2514\u2500 Codec decodes bytes\n   \u2514\u2500 Codec calls ServerConnectionCallbacks::newStream()\n\n3. ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream() creates ActiveStream\n   \u2514\u2500 ActiveStream creates FilterManager\n   \u2514\u2500 FilterManager creates filters (via FilterChainFactory)\n\n4. Codec calls ActiveStream::decodeHeaders()\n   \u2193\n5. ActiveStream::decodeHeaders() \u2192 FilterManager::decodeHeaders()\n   \u2193\n6. FilterManager iterates decoder filters:\n   Filter[0]::decodeHeaders() \u2192 Filter[1]::decodeHeaders() \u2192 ... \u2192 Router Filter::decodeHeaders()\n\n7. Router Filter:\n   \u251c\u2500 Selects route from RouteConfiguration\n   \u251c\u2500 Resolves cluster name\n   \u251c\u2500 Gets ThreadLocalCluster from ClusterManager\n   \u251c\u2500 Calls LoadBalancer::chooseHost() \u2192 selects endpoint\n   \u251c\u2500 Requests connection pool from cluster: cluster->httpConnPool()\n   \u2514\u2500 Creates UpstreamRequest(conn_pool)\n\n8. UpstreamRequest registers as pool callbacks:\n   \u2514\u2500 Waits for onPoolReady() or onPoolFailure()\n\n9. Connection pool processing:\n   \u251c\u2500 If idle connection available: call onPoolReady() immediately\n   \u251c\u2500 If no idle connection:\n   \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Create new TCP connection (if under max_connections)\n   \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Initialize HTTP codec\n   \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Call onPoolReady(upstream)\n   \u2514\u2500 If max connections reached: queue in pending list\n\n10. UpstreamRequest::onPoolReady():\n    \u251c\u2500 Registers for upstream codec events\n    \u251c\u2500 Creates upstream filter manager\n    \u251c\u2500 Calls acceptHeadersFromRouter()\n    \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Passes headers through upstream filter manager\n    \u2502  \u2514\u2500 UpstreamCodecFilter encodes to upstream codec\n    \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Data sent on upstream TCP connection\n    \u2514\u2500 Waits for response\n\n11. Codec processes body data:\n    Codec \u2192 ActiveStream::decodeData() \u2192 FilterManager::decodeData()\n    \u2192 (decoder filters process, may buffer/modify/stop)\n    \u2192 Router Filter::decodeData() \u2192 UpstreamRequest::acceptDataFromRouter()\n    \u2192 (upstream filters) \u2192 UpstreamCodecFilter \u2192 upstream codec \u2192 wire\n```\n\n### Upstream Response Path\n\n```\n1. Upstream server sends response\n   \u2193\n2. Upstream TCP connection receives data\n   \u2514\u2500 Upstream codec decodes bytes\n   \u2514\u2500 Upstream codec calls UpstreamCodecFilter callbacks\n\n3. UpstreamCodecFilter (terminal upstream filter) calls:\n   UpstreamRequest::decodeHeaders/Data/Trailers()\n   \u2193\n4. UpstreamRequest passes through upstream filter manager (reverse order)\n   \u2514\u2500 Filters can modify, buffer, or stop iteration\n   \u2193\n5. UpstreamRequest signals back to Router Filter:\n   onUpstreamHeaders() \u2192 onUpstreamData() \u2192 onUpstreamTrailers()\n   \u2193\n6. Router Filter calls FilterManager to encode response:\n   Filter1::encodeHeaders() \u2190 Filter2::encodeHeaders() \u2190 ... \u2190 Router\n   (Note: encoder chain is reversed)\n   \u2193\n7. FilterManager sends encoded response downstream:\n   ActiveStream::encodeHeaders() \u2192 Codec::encodeHeaders()\n   \u2193\n8. Codec sends response bytes on downstream TCP connection\n   \u2193\n9. Client receives response\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\nEnvoy's HCM provides several mechanisms for customization:\n\n### 1. HTTP Filters\n\nFilters are the primary extension mechanism. They can:\n- **Decoder filters**: Inspect/modify requests, add request headers, stop iteration\n- **Encoder filters**: Inspect/modify responses, add response headers\n- **Terminal filters**: Make forwarding decisions (Router filter is an example)\n\nFilter types:\n```cpp\n// Decoder-only\nclass StreamDecoderFilter { ... };\n\n// Encoder-only\nclass StreamEncoderFilter { ... };\n\n// Dual-mode (both decoder and encoder)\nclass StreamFilter : public StreamDecoderFilter, public StreamEncoderFilter { ... };\n```\n\nCommon filters:\n- **Router**: Forwards to upstream clusters\n- **Authentication (auth)**: Validates JWTs, OAuth tokens\n- **Rate limiting**: Enforces per-second request limits\n- **Buffer**: Buffers request body for inspection\n- **Lua**: Scripted request/response manipulation\n- **Access log**: Logs requests after completion\n- **Compression**: Compresses response body\n- **Header rewrite**: Adds/removes/modifies headers\n\n### 2. Route Configuration\n\nThe RouteConfiguration specifies:\n- Virtual hosts (domain matching)\n- Routes (path matching, method matching, header matching)\n- Per-route actions:\n  - Cluster name\n  - Timeout policy\n  - Retry policy\n  - Weighted clusters (load balancing across multiple clusters)\n  - Redirect rules\n  - Direct response (bypass upstream)\n  - Per-route filter config (enable/disable/configure filters)\n\n### 3. Cluster Extensions\n\nClusters are extensible:\n- **Load balancing policies**: Custom LB algorithms\n- **Connection pool factories**: Different protocol implementations (HTTP/1, HTTP/2, gRPC, etc.)\n- **Health checkers**: Active health check implementations\n- **Outlier detection**: Custom failure detection algorithms\n\n### 4. Codec Extensions\n\nNew HTTP protocol versions or variants can be plugged in:\n- HTTP/1.1: `source/common/http/http1/`\n- HTTP/2: `source/common/http/http2/`\n- HTTP/3 (QUIC): `source/common/http/http3/`\n\nEach implements the `Http::Connection` interface for codec creation and the `Http::CodecFactory` for instantiation.\n\n### 5. Access Logging\n\nAccess logs are specified in HCM configuration and filters:\n- Format string with variable substitution (request headers, response headers, response time, etc.)\n- Multiple log destinations (files, gRPC, etc.)\n- Filter expressions to conditionally log\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling and Recovery\n\n### Codec Errors\n\nIf the HTTP codec encounters invalid data (bad request line, malformed headers):\n1. Codec signals error via `StreamDecoderFilterCallbacks::sendLocalReply()`\n2. HCM generates a 400 Bad Request response\n3. Response is sent to client\n4. Connection may be closed (depending on protocol and error severity)\n\n### Filter Errors\n\nIf a filter encounters an error during processing:\n- Filter calls `sendLocalReply()` with appropriate error code\n- FilterManager stops executing further decoder filters\n- Response is sent downstream\n- Router filter is notified via `onLocalReply()` to clean up upstream resources\n\n### Upstream Connection Failures\n\nIf the connection pool fails to establish a connection:\n1. UpstreamRequest::onPoolFailure() is called with failure reason\n2. Router filter checks retry policy\n3. If retries available:\n   - Create new UpstreamRequest\n   - Attempt same headers/data on different host or cluster\n4. If no retries or all attempts fail:\n   - Router sends local reply (503 Service Unavailable)\n   - Response sent to client\n\n### Upstream Stream Resets\n\nIf the upstream stream resets mid-transmission:\n1. UpstreamRequest is notified\n2. Router filter is notified via onResetStream()\n3. Router checks if retry is possible\n4. If yes: create new UpstreamRequest and retry\n5. If no: reset downstream stream or send local reply\n\n### Timeout Handling\n\n**Per-try timeout**:\n- Set by UpstreamRequest when forwarding headers\n- If upstream doesn't respond within timeout, connection/stream is reset\n- Triggers retry if allowed\n\n**Global request timeout**:\n- Set by router filter based on route config\n- Applies to entire request (all retries combined)\n- If exceeded, downstream stream is reset with timeout error\n\n---\n\n## Performance Considerations\n\n### 1. Memory Efficiency\n\n- **ActiveStream pooling**: Streams are allocated on-demand and deferred-deleted to avoid allocation during busy periods\n- **Filter buffering**: Data is buffered in memory-aware buffers that track allocation\n- **Connection pooling**: Idle connections are kept in pools to avoid connection setup overhead\n\n### 2. Request Pipelining\n\n- **HTTP/1.1**: Requests are processed sequentially; pipelining is supported but requires careful ordering\n- **HTTP/2**: Multiple streams per connection are multiplexed at codec level\n- **Connection reuse**: Keep-alive connections reduce latency\n\n### 3. Watermarks and Backpressure\n\n- **Read watermarks**: When buffers fill, reading is disabled to prevent memory exhaustion\n- **Write watermarks**: When downstream write buffers fill, upstream reading is disabled\n- **Filter-level watermarks**: Filters can signal back-pressure when they can't process data\n\n### 4. Load Balancing Efficiency\n\n- **Sticky sessions**: Consistent hashing keeps client requests on same upstream\n- **Locality awareness**: Prefers nearby endpoints to reduce latency\n- **Connection multiplexing**: HTTP/2 multiplexing allows many requests per connection\n\n---\n\n## Key Source Files\n\n### Connection Management\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/cc`: ConnectionManagerImpl and ActiveStream\n- `source/common/http/conn_manager_config.h`: Configuration interface\n\n### Filter Chain\n- `source/common/http/filter_manager.h/cc`: FilterManager, stream filter wrappers\n- `source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h`: Filter creation utilities\n- `envoy/http/filter.h`: Filter interface definitions\n\n### Routing\n- `source/common/router/router.h/cc`: Router filter implementation\n- `source/common/router/config_impl.h/cc`: Route configuration and matching\n- `source/common/router/upstream_request.h/cc`: UpstreamRequest lifecycle\n- `source/extensions/filters/http/router/config.cc`: Router filter factory\n\n### Cluster Management\n- `envoy/upstream/cluster_manager.h`: ClusterManager interface\n- `source/common/upstream/cluster_manager_impl.h/cc`: ClusterManagerImpl\n- `source/common/upstream/cluster_impl.h/cc`: Cluster and host management\n- `source/common/upstream/load_balancer_impl.h/cc`: Load balancer algorithms\n\n### Codecs\n- `source/common/http/http1/codec_impl.h/cc`: HTTP/1.1 codec\n- `source/common/http/http2/codec_impl.h/cc`: HTTP/2 codec\n- `source/common/http/http3/`: HTTP/3 (QUIC) codec\n\n### Connection Pools\n- `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h/cc`: HTTP connection pool base\n- `source/common/http/http1/conn_pool.h/cc`: HTTP/1.1 connection pool\n- `source/common/http/http2/conn_pool.h/cc`: HTTP/2 connection pool\n\n---\n\n## References\n\nThis document covers the core HCM architecture for HTTP request processing. For additional detail:\n\n1. **Dynamic Configuration (xDS)**: See CDS (Cluster Discovery Service) and RDS (Route Discovery Service) for how routes and clusters are updated at runtime\n2. **Tracing**: HCM integrates with OpenTelemetry/Jaeger for distributed tracing\n3. **Metrics**: HCM emits detailed metrics for requests, connections, upstream hosts\n4. **TLS/SSL**: HCM supports both downstream and upstream TLS with certificate management and validation\n5. **Virtual Hosts and Scoped Routes**: Advanced routing features for multi-tenancy and version management\n",

: public Network::ReadFilter,\n                             public ServerConnectionCallbacks,\n                             public Network::ConnectionCallbacks,\n                             public Http::ApiListener\n```\n\nThe class serves multiple roles:\n- **Network::ReadFilter**: Receives raw socket data via `onData()` and `onNewConnection()`\n- **ServerConnectionCallbacks**: Implements Management\n\nWhen a new HTTP stream arrives, the codec calls `newStream()` to create an **ActiveStream**, which wraps a single request/response pair:\n\n```cpp\nstruct ActiveStream : public     public RequestDecoder,\n                      public Tracing::Config,\n                      public FilterManagerCallbacks,\n                      public DownstreamStreamFilterCallbacks,\n                      public RouteCache\n```\n\nEach **ActiveStream**:\n- Holds the HTTP codec's `ResponseEncoder` for sending responses downstream\n- Contains a `FilterManager` instance that executes the filter chain\n- Manages stream-level state: headers, trailers, metadata, body data\n- Implements request decoder interface for receiving codec events\n- Acts as `FilterManagerCallbacks` to receive filter-produced output (headers, data, trailers)\n- Implements `DownstreamStreamFilterCallbacks` for filter-to-HCM signaling (route updates, timeouts)\n\n#### 1.4 Connection-Level Concerns\n\n**Flow ConnectionManagerImpl propagates these to all active streams\n- Streams use watermarks to signal back-pressure to upstream hosts\n\n**Drain Management**:\n- ConnectionManagerImpl monitors the `Network::DrainDecision` to detect when the server is draining\n- During drain, no new HTTP/2 streams are accepted on the connection (HTTP/1.1 connections complete in-flight requests then close)\n\n**Overload Protection**:\n- Integrates with `Server::OverloadManager` to detect resource exhaustion\n- Can stop accepting new streams or close connections when overloaded\n- Tracks premature stream resets and can drain connections based on reset ratios\n\n#### 1.5 Codec Selection Architecture\n\nThe codec is selected lazily based on the first data received. This is important because:\n- The protocol might not be known until bytes arrive (except for H3 where QUIC's stream setup provides the info)\n- Different protocols have different multiplexing and streaming semantics\n- The codec drives all downstream behavior through callback interfaces\n\n---",

# Envoy HTTP Connection Manager Architecture

## Overview

The HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) is Envoy's core subsystem for processing HTTP requests from downstream clients, transforming them according to configured routing and filtering rules, and forwarding them to upstream services. This document explains the design and interactions between the four major components that implement this functionality.

The HCM request processing pipeline follows this flow:
1. **Raw bytes arrive** on a downstream TCP connection
2. **ConnectionManagerImpl** (Network::ReadFilter) receives and decodes them
3. **ActiveStream** is created per request and manages per-stream state
4. **FilterManager** executes the configured HTTP filter chain
5. **Router Filter** (terminal decoder filter) performs route selection and upstream forwarding
6. **UpstreamRequest** manages the upstream connection and stream lifecycle
7. **ClusterManager** and **ThreadLocalCluster** provide connection pools to upstream services
8. **Responses flow back** through the filter chain in reverse order

---

## 1. ConnectionManagerImpl: The Network Filter Entry Point

### Location
- Header: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h`
- Implementation: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`

### Responsibilities

**ConnectionManagerImpl** is the primary entry point for HTTP request processing. It is a `Network::ReadFilter` that lives on each downstream TCP connection and orchestrates the entire request lifecycle.

#### 1.1 Connection-Level Ownership

```cpp
class ConnectionManagerImpl : public Network::ReadFilter,
                             public ServerConnectionCallbacks,
                             public Network::ConnectionCallbacks,
                             public Http::ApiListener
```

The class serves multiple
